State v. Nelson


NO. 73031


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 6304



December 23, 1999, Date of Announcement of Decision


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Criminal appeal from Common Pleas Court. Case No. CR-244838.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant brought this appeal from the Common Pleas Court, Cuyahoga County (Ohio), which designated him a sexual predator under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.09(B)(1).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted for the rape of a five-year-old boy. The trial court subsequently determined appellant to be a sexual predator. Appellant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence used by the trial court to designate him as a sexual predator. Appellant claimed that the sole evidence before the court in the sexual predator hearing was old conviction data. However, the trial court considered the nature of the offense, the presentence investigation report, and the age of the victim. Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.09(B) (2) did not require that all listed factors be met. Evidence was sufficient to support trial court's determination.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. Trial court made determination based on nature of the offense, the presentence investigation report, and the age of the victim, in conformance with statutory requirements. Evidence supported sexual predator determination.

Berge v. Columbus Community Cable Access


Nos. 99AP-75 and 99AP-76


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


136 Ohio App. 3d 281; 736 N.E.2d 517; 1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 6455



December 23, 1999, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended February 6, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from a judgment of the Franklin County Common Pleas Court (Ohio), granting defendant employer a new trial following a jury verdict for plaintiff on his claim of handicap discrimination, a directed verdict to defendant building landlord, and summary judgment to defendant city.


OVERVIEW: During the course of plaintiff paraplegic's employment by defendant, he experienced various difficulties due to lack of handicap accessibility to the building. Plaintiff sued defendant for injuries he sustained while another employee was helping plaintiff down the front steps of defendant's building. At trial, the jury returned a monetary verdict for plaintiff. The trial court then granted defendant's motion for a new trial, finding the verdict against the weight of the evidence. On appeal, the court concluded that the trial court's failure to instruct on punitive damages was not plain error, the trial court could not consider the juror's affidavit to determine if jury's award was result of passion or prejudice since the affidavit failed to demonstrate personal knowledge of anything improper the jury considered, and that the trial court's decision to grant new trial upon finding plaintiff's evidence on pain and suffering was insufficient to warrant extra damages was not abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded. Trial court's decision to grant defendant's motion for new trial upon finding that plaintiff's evidence on pain and suffering were not sufficient to warrant jury's award of damages was not abuse of discretion.

State v. Spingola


Case No. 99CA19


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, ATHENS COUNTY


136 Ohio App. 3d 136; 736 N.E.2d 48; 1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 6290



December 22, 1999, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Judgment of trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed an appeal challenging a judgment of the Athens County Municipal Court (Ohio), which convicted him of criminal trespassing on a public university's grounds.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was arrested after refusing to leave a public university's property. Appellant had been preaching at a monument on campus where assemblies and public speaking were prohibited by university policy. As he preached, appellant engaged in heated dialogue with several students, and was subsequently asked to leave. Appellant was convicted of criminal trespass. On appeal, appellant argued he had an U.S. Const. amend. I privilege to preach at the monument because it was a public forum. He also contended the university selectively enforced its permit requirement based on the speaker's viewpoint and that the university's policy on speech was unconstitutionally vague. The court affirmed the conviction, holding, inter alia, appellant had no U.S. Const. amend. I right to engage in public communication at the monument because it was a non-public forum and the university's policy restricting loud speech to groups of individuals at the monument served the university's educational mission.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; appellant had no constitutional privilege to preach on public university property because location of his communication had been designated a non-public forum for the reasonable purpose of advancing the university's educational mission of maintaining a quiet academic setting.

Casto v. Village of Commer. Point


Case No. 99 CA 2


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, PICKAWAY COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 6353



December 22, 1999, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [*1] JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from a Pickaway County Common Pleas Court (Ohio) judgment upholding a decision by the Commercial Point Zoning Appeals Board, to deny a request by plaintiff to construct a car wash on property he owned in the Village of Commercial Point.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought to build a car wash on land zoned for business, but on which a nonconforming residence stood. The trial court denied appellant's zoning appeal because the zoning ordinances barred residences that were not located in the principal use building. The appellate court agreed that the residence would not be in the car wash. The court held such limitations on usage were a reasonable means of promoting the general welfare of the community. The court held that a zoning ordinance would not be struck down unless it was shown to be clearly arbitrary and unreasonable and without substantial relation to the public health, safety, morals or general welfare of the community. This onerous standard to meet was not met by appellants.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because the judgment denying request to build car wash was not arbitrary, unreasonable or unconscionable. Limiting residences to within principal use business building was reasonable means of promoting the general welfare of the community.

State v. Ingledue


CASE NO. 97-CO-55


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, COLUMBIANA COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 6425



December 22, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at, Decision reached on appeal by State v. Ingledue, 2014-Ohio-4003, 2014 Ohio App. LEXIS 3918 (Ohio Ct. App., Columbiana County, Sept. 8, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Criminal Appeal from Columbiana County Common Pleas Court. Case No. 87 CR 118.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed an appeal from a judgment rendered by the Columbiana County Common Pleas Court (Ohio) classifying appellant as a sexual predator, thereby requiring him to register in accordance with Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.03.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of rape, and gross sexual imposition. The Ohio Department of Rehabilitation and Correction recommended that appellant be classified as a sexual predator. The trial court conducted a hearing pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.09 to determine whether appellant was a sexual predator. The trial court found appellant to be a sexual predator, and further held that he was subject to the notification requirements of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.03. The appellate court held that the sexual predator statute was constitutional. The statute did not violate the prohibitions against ex post facto laws, the retroactive laws, the double jeopardy provisions, or the equal protection clause of the U.S. Const. amend. XIV. Nor was the statute unconstitutionally vague. Also, the record substantiated the decision to find appellant a sexual predator.


OUTCOME: The trial court's ruling was affirmed because the sexual predator statute was not unconstitutional, and the evidence supported the determination that appellant was a sexual predator.

State v. Bristow

December 21, 1999, Date of Judgment Entry

DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged denial, by the Common Pleas Court of Crawford County (Ohio), of his motion to withdraw guilty pleas.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of 14 counts of telephone harassment and indicted for harassment by inmate and aiding escape. During imposition of the sentence on the telephone harassment convictions, appellant suggested a negotiated plea under which he would plead guilty to aiding escape and harassment by inmate, would have his probation revoked, and would agree to be determined a vexatious litigator. In an earlier appeal, the court held Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2323.52, the vexatious litigator statute, was unconstitutional. Appellant later moved to withdraw his guilty pleas. State v. Loop


CASE NO. CA98-10-017


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TWELFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FAYETTE COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 6093



December 20, 1999, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [*1] Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Fayette County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) convicting him of speeding in violation of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 4511.21(D)(2).


OVERVIEW: Appellant claimed that the complaint was defective because the ticket issued to appellant was not verified by a sufficient affidavit and was not issued by a prosecuting attorney. These arguments were previously addressed and rejected by appellate courts throughout Ohio. Appellee state filed a bill of particulars with the trial court on September 28, 1998 and served a copy on appellant. The Ohio Uniform Traffic Ticket charged appellant with a violation of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 4511.21 and was therefore sufficient to invoke the trial court's jurisdiction. Previous courts had rejected arguments that the statute was invalid because there was not enacting clause in the legislation. Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 4511.21 was not unconstitutional for noncompliance with provisions of Ohio Const. art. II.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed; prior appellate courts rejected appellant's arguments; the traffic ticket charged appellant with a violation of the statue which was sufficient to invoke the trial court's jurisdiction; statute was constitutional.

 

310 of 2888 DOCUMENTS


Stevens v. Ackman


CASE NO. CA99-03-053


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TWELFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, BUTLER COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 6109



December 20, 1999, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [*1] Judgment reversed and summary judgment entered in favor of the city of Middletown.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, city of Middletown, appealed an order of the Butler County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which overruled its motion for summary judgment on the basis of statutory political subdivision immunity in plaintiff; administratrix of decedent's estate, who, after a fatal traffic accident, filed a wrongful death action.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed a wrongful death action against defendant, city of Middletown, alleging an improperly maintained berm caused a fatal traffic accident. The court found that jurisdiction vested under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2505.02(B)(2) because the "underlying action" was a "special proceeding" because a civil claim for wrongful death and survivorship was unknown at common law and did not exist in law or equity prior to 1853. The court held that the maintenance of the berm did not constitute a nuisance within the meaning of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2744.02(B)(3). The edge drop in this case was not analogous to a significant chuckhole or pothole on or adjacent to a roadway, nor did it constitute an obstruction to a driver's normal visibility within the right of way. The court found that an edge drop on a city road was not a failure to keep the road free from nuisance.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and summary judgment entered in favor of defendant city; statutory exception to political subdivision immunity did not apply as maintenance of berm was not nuisance as a matter of law. Jurisdiction was proper as special proceeding because wrongful death and survivorship actions were unknown at common law.

State v. Everly


Case No. 1999CA00125


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, STARK COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 6311



December 20, 1999, Date of Judgment Entry


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Criminal Appeal from Stark County Court of Common Pleas. Case No. 88-8643.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from judgment of the Stark County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), adjudicating him a sexual predator as defined in Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.01(E), maintaining he was deprived of due process by not continuing his hearing, and the finding was not supported by clear and convincing evidence.


OVERVIEW: After enactment of Ohio's version of Megan's Law, Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950, defendant was found to be a sexual predator. The court held that registration and notification provisions of the statute did not violate the ex post facto clause because its provisions served the remedial purpose of protecting the public. The court found the trial court did not deprive appellant of his right to due process by denying appellant's oral motion for a continuance and holding the sexual predator hearing since defendant could petition the court to reclassify him based on his subsequent remedial behavior. Defendant exhibited a "pattern of abuse" with respect to his two victims, thus, the finding of defendant as a sexual predator was supported by clear and convincing evidence and was not against the weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because defendant was a sexual predator by clear and convincing evidence and finding was not against the manifest weight of the evidence. Defendant not deprived of due process by denying his oral motion for a continuance of sexual predator hearing since defendant could petition to reclassify his status.

State v. Pavlick


Case No. 98-CA-002


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, HOLMES COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 6372



December 20, 1999, Date of Judgment Entry


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Criminal Appeal from Holmes County Court of Common Pleas. Case No. 96-CR-022.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed an appeal challenging a judgment of the Holmes County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) adjudicating her a sexual predator as defined in Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.01(E).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of corruption of a minor and was placed on probation. The trial court later adjudicated appellant, 19, a sexual predator pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950 et seq. after the presentence investigation indicated that appellant had sexual intercourse and/or sexual contact with five juvenile boys ranging in age from 13 to 15 during a short period of time. Appellant had stated that she did not think she knew how to say no. On appeal, appellant argued that § 2950 violated the constitution because it unreasonably interfered with appellant's liberty beyond the necessities of the situation. The court affirmed, holding that government dissemination of information regarding appellant's status as a sexual predator was not unconstitutional because it served the paramount governmental interest of protecting members of the public from sex offenders. The offender's conviction for a sexual crime had always been a matter of public record.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; the trial court decision to adjudicate appellant a sexual predator was supported by clear and convincing evidence. Statutory requirement that government publish information regarding appellant's status as a sexual predator was not unconstitutional because it was aimed at protecting the public from sex offenders.

State v. Boughner


ACCELERATED CASE NO. 98-G-2161


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, GEAUGA COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 6116



December 17, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Criminal Appeal from the Chardon Municipal Court. Case No. 97 CRB 001123.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Modified and affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his convictions for aggravated menacing and resisting arrest following a trial by jury in the Chardon Municipal Court (Ohio).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with aggravated menacing, resisting arrest, and using a weapon while intoxicated, and a public defender was appointed to represent him. The day before trial, counsel moved for leave to withdraw; the motion was granted, and appellant given a two-week continuance to retain counsel. At the next hearing, appellant was still unrepresented, and allegedly requested the trial court to appoint substitute counsel, which was denied. At trial, appellant defended himself pro se, was convicted of aggravated menacing and resisting arrest, and sentenced to 180 days imprisonment and fines. On appeal, the court ruled the trial court did not comply with Ohio R. Crim. P. 44 and 22; the record did not reflect that appellant entered a valid waiver of his right to be represented by counsel at trial, thus violating his right to counsel. Therefore, the court vacated the jail sentence, but affirmed the conviction and fines.


OUTCOME: Judgment modified and affirmed as modified; where record did not reflect that appellant entered valid waiver of his right to be represented by counsel at trial, his right to counsel was violated, thus his jail sentence was vacated, but convictions for aggravated menacing and resisting arrest and fines were affirmed.

George Shima Buick, Inc. v. Ferencak


ACCELERATED CASE NOS. 98-L-202


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LAKE COUNTY

December 17, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Civil Appeal from the Painesville Municipal Court. Case No. 98 CVI 00762.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Painesville Municipal Court (Ohio), that granted default judgment to appellee company after appellant filed a complaint against appellee for stopping payment on a check.


OVERVIEW: Appellant claimed that Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 1925.17 was unconstitutional because it violated the separation of powers doctrine of Ohio's Constitution. The court found that Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 1925.17 did not usurp the supreme court's authority to make rules governing the courts or the practice of law in Ohio but was excluded by Ohio R. Civ. P. 1(C)(4), and pursuant to Ohio Const. art. IV, § 5(B). The record indicated that the trial court ruled on appellant's motion, went forward with the trial, and ruled in favor of appellee, due to appellant's absence. Nothing indicated that the trial date was ever continued or that the trial court acted improperly.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed; the statute was not unconstitutional, as it did not usurp the court's authority to make rules governing the courts or the practice of law in Ohio; trial court did not act improperly in moving forward with trial and ruling in favor of appellee.

State v. Schlee


CASE NO. 98-L-187


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LAKE COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 6136



December 17, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Civil Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 92 CR 000517.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed an appeal to a final judgment of the Lake County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which denied appellant's second petition for postconviction relief without an evidentiary hearing.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, convicted of aggravated murder, was sentenced to life in prison. Appellant's petition for postconviction relief was denied. The court reversed and remanded the trial court's denial of appellant's first petition without a hearing. Appellant appealed from the trial court's denial of his second postconviction relief petition, alleging denial of due process because no evidentiary hearing was held, and Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2953.23 was unconstitutional because it required a higher standard of proof than required for Brady violations. The court affirmed, holding that under the statute, the trial court could not entertain a subsequent petition unless the petitioner showed by clear and convincing evidence that, but for constitutional error at trial, no reasonable factfinder would have found the petitioner guilty of the offense of which he was convicted. Appellant did not raise the question of the statute's constitutionality in his postconviction relief petition, therefore it was waived.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. Appellant did not question the statute's constitutionality in his petition, therefore it was waived. Additionally, the trial court could not entertain a subsequent petition unless clear and convincing evidence showed that, but for constitutional error at trial, no reasonable factfinder would have found appellant guilty.

 

316 of 2888 DOCUMENTS


Midwest Fireworks Mfg. Co. v. Deerfield Twp. Bd. of Zoning Appeals


CASE NO. 98-P-0131


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, PORTAGE COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 6142



December 17, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Upon Review Affirmed December 21, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Ohio App. LEXIS 5861.


PRIOR HISTORY: CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Administrative Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas. Case No. 98 CV 0272.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Reversed and judgment entered for appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant fireworks manufacturer appealed the judgment entered by the Portage County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which affirmed the decision of appellee zoning appeals board to revoke a zoning certificate issued to appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's fireworks factory was on 86 acres of land across a highway from appellee landowner's property. Appellant's property was zoned as a residential district, but has been an allowed non-conforming use. Fifteen years after two buildings were destroyed, appellant was granted a zoning certificate to replace them. Twenty days later, appellee landowner filed an appeal by delivering it to the township clerk. After a hearing, appellee board revoked the certificate; appellant filed an administrative appeal with the trial court, which affirmed. On appeal, the court reversed. Although the appellee board had jurisdiction, the notice requirement was fulfilled, and all proper parties were notified of the hearing, appellee landowner did not show how a new building would affect his personal, pecuniary or property rights, and therefore he was not a "person aggrieved." Since appellee landowner had no standing to appeal, the appellee board had no authority to revoke the zoning certificate.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and entered for appellant; although appellee board had jurisdiction over the matter and notice requirements were met, appellee landowner was not a "person aggrieved"; he did not show how appellant's new building would affect his personal, pecuniary or property rights and therefore he lacked standing to appeal.

State v. Wilburn


Case No. 97CA586


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, HOLMES COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 6313



December 17, 1999, Date of Judgment Entry


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas. Case No. 91CR056.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Holmes County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), adjudicating him as a sexual predator as defined in Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.01(E).


OVERVIEW: In 1991, appellant pled guilty to aiding and abetting felonious sexual penetration. In 1997, appellant was adjudicated to be a sexual predator, pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.09. Appellant argued on appeal that such application violated his rights as an ex post facto law, and under Ohio Const. art. I, § 1, and the determination was not supported by clear and convincing evidence. The court affirmed. Previous caselaw, holding the statute constitutional, was dispositive of the first claim and persuasive of the second. The dissemination requirement did not impinge on any reasonable expectation of finality defendant may have had, and registration imposed a de minimis administrative inconvenience. Upon reviewing the evidence and the Ohio Rev. Code Ann. 2950.09(B)(2) factors, the trial court's conclusion that appellant should be classified as a sexual predator was supported by clear and convincing evidence and not against the manifest weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; sexual predator determination was supported by clear and convincing evidence and not against the manifest weight of the evidence; sexual predator law was constitutional, not ex post facto law, and did not unreasonably interfere with appellant's liberty.

DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner criminal defendant appealed the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas, Cuyahoga County (Ohio), denying his petition for post-conviction relief, in favor of respondent state, from his 1975 convictions for aggravated robbery and murder.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner contended that the trial court erred in dismissing the postconviction proceeding, because his murder conviction was void, as it violated certain amendments of the United States Constitution. OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed; there was no violation of the United States Constitution in the conviction; petitioner's guilty plea had been properly entered; petitioner failed to demonstrate ineffective assistance of counsel and his intelligence was considered during the trial.

321 of 2888 DOCUMENTS


State v. Grundy


Case No. 99CA0046


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LICKING COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 6184



December 14, 1999, Date of Judgment Entry


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas. Case No. 98CR445.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas Licking County (Ohio) convicting him of one count of domestic violence in violation of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2919.25(A) because of an incident involving appellant's daughter, and using a prior 1991 conviction to enhance the charge to a felony.


OVERVIEW: Appellant attempted to bar the trial court from using his 1991 conviction to enhance the current charge of domestic violence to a felony. Appellant was not indigent at the time of the 1991 case and there was no evidence that appellant had waived his right to counsel. The absence of the waiver of trial counsel coupled with the fact that appellant was not indigent was not a constitutional impediment to the enhancement of the charge from a misdemeanor to a felony. The court held that an uncounseled misdemeanor conviction could be used under the enhancement provision of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2913.02(B) to convert the subsequent misdemeanor into a felony when no actual imprisonment resulted. Based upon the facts where there was no proof of indigency, no imprisonment in the predicate misdemeanor, and no waiver of counsel, the trial court was correct in sentencing appellant for a felony domestic violence conviction.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. The fact that appellant was not indigent and did not waive his right to counsel were not constitutional impediments to use the prior 1991 misdemeanor conviction for domestic violence to enhance the current charge to a felony because imprisonment did not result from appellant's 1991 conviction.

State v. Berry

323 of 2888 DOCUMENTS


Ackerman v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co.


APPEAL NO. C-990332


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, HAMILTON COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 5886



December 10, 1999, Date of Judgment Entry on Appeal


NOTICE:

 [*1] THESE ARE NOT OFFICIAL HEADNOTES AND OR SYLLABI AND ARE NEITHER APPROVED IN ADVANCE NOR ENDORSED BY THE COURT. PLEASE REVIEW THE CASE IN FULL.


PRIOR HISTORY: Civil Appeal From: Hamilton County Common Pleas Court. TRIAL NO. A-9803653.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Appealed From Is: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appellants sought review of summary judgment order in favor of defendant insurer from Hamilton County Common Pleas Court (Ohio) in a declaratory judgment action seeking an additional $ 200,000 under the per-accident limits of their uninsured-motorist coverage and a declaration that Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 3937.18 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff-appellants contended that the liability limits in their auto insurance policy was unconstitutional. The court distinguished civil damages and a claim under an insurance policy. Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 3937.18(H) did not violate Ohio Const. art. I § 19a because the statute did not limit civil damages in a wrongful death action. The statute applied to the contractual agreement between the insurer and the insured, and permitted insurers to limit recovery of uninsured-motorist benefits. While the plaintiff-appellants were limited in the amount they may recover from defendant because of the contractual terms of their insurance policy, they were not limited in the amount of damages they could recover from the culpable motorist. Because Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 3937.18(H) created no classification, there was no discrimination that would implicate the equal protection clauses of either the United States or the Ohio Constitution.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. While plaintiffs were limited in the amount they may recover from defendant because of contractual terms of their insurance policy, they were not limited in the amount of damages they could recover from the culpable motorist.

State v. Schofield


Case No. 99 CA 10


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, WASHINGTON COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 6095



December 10, 1999, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [*1] JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction of driving under the influence, Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 4511.19(A), in Washington County Common Pleas Court, alleging acceptance of guilty plea was involuntary, ineffective assistance of counsel and improper sentencing.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charging with violating Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 4511.19(A), driving under the influence of alcohol to which appellant pled guilty. Some months later, appellant was sentenced to jail, an alcohol rehabilitation center, and three years community control. The appellate court affirmed both the conviction and sentence, holding that the trial court fully complied with provisions of Ohio Crim. R. 11 in accepting appellant's knowing and voluntary plea. Moreover, Ohio Crim. R. 23(A) and Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2945.05 regarding written waivers of jury trials were inapplicable to guilty pleas. The appellate court further rejected appellant's argument that trial counsel's performance was deficient because appellant failed to explain how foreknowledge of the urine analysis would have affected his decision to plead guilty and the sentence, within the statutory guidelines, was not improper merely because the trial court failed to use the words, "mandatory term," in its sentencing entry.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed because the trial court fully complied with required procedures in accepting guilty plea. Written waivers of jury trials were inapplicable to guilty pleas. Trial counsel's performance was presumed effective when appellant failed to specify how counsel's performance negatively impacted his ability to enter a voluntary plea.

Watkins v. Ohio Dep't of Rehabilitation & Correction


No. 99AP-300


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 5846



December 9, 1999, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed the judgment of the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which granted motion to dismiss defendants Ohio Department of Rehabilitation and Correction, State of Ohio, Ohio Criminal Sentencing Commission and judge.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed suit against defendants Ohio Department of Rehabilitation and Correction, State of Ohio, Ohio Criminal Sentencing Commission and judge, alleging that he was improperly incarcerated because the passage of Am.Sub.S.B. No. 2 abolished all of the laws under which he was being held, and seeking monetary damages. Defendants' motion to dismiss was granted, and plaintiff appealed. Because plaintiff's complaint failed to state any claim upon which relief could be granted against defendants, the judgment was affirmed. On plaintiff's assertion that he was entitled to immediate release due to the changes made by Am.Sub.S.B. No. 2, the proper action for him to file was a habeas corpus action. Plaintiff's contention that Am.Sub.S.B. No. 2 was unconstitutional was unpersuasive, given that the Ohio Supreme Court had already determined that Am.Sub.S.B. No. 2 did not violate the constitutional prohibition against ex post facto and retroactive legislation.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed, because plaintiff failed to state a claim upon which relief could be granted, given that he should have filed a habeas corpus action to seek his release from incarceration, and that Am.Sub.S.B. No. 2 had previously been determined constitutional.

Summary judgment grant on medical malpractice claim reversed, because medical malpractice certificate of merit statute had been declared unconstitutional.

State v. Brock

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Criminal appeal from Common Pleas Court. No. CR-362419.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: CONVICTION VACATED AND DEFENDANT DISCHARGED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed a criminal appeal from the conviction and sentence entered by the Cuyahoga County Common Pleas Court (Ohio) for the crime of drug possession after the trial court denied appellant's motion to suppress.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with one count of drug possession. He entered a plea of no contest after the trial court denied his motion to suppress. On appeal, appellant asserted that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress and in granting his motion for return of funds, but ordering that the funds be deposited with the clerk of courts and applied to outstanding court costs. The appellate court agreed. The evidence derived from the illegal stop was therefore inadmissible. Appellant's conviction was vacated. Also, costs of prosecution could not be ordered against appellant, since the court vacated appellant's conviction.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction was vacated, and appellant was discharged. The investigatory stop was unlawful since there was no founded suspicion that appellant was engaged in any criminal activity.

City of Cleveland v. Mathis


NO. 76470


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


136 Ohio App. 3d 41; 735 N.E.2d 949; 1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 5897



December 9, 1999, Date of Announcement of Decision


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended February 6, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Criminal appeal from the Cleveland Municipal Court. Case No. 99 CRB-001543.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Reversed and Vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged her conviction by the Cleveland Municipal Court (Ohio) for loitering for the purpose of engaging in prostitution, a violation of Cleveland, Ohio Codified Ordinance 619.1.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled no contest to the violation of Cleveland, Ohio Codified Ordinance 619.11, loitering for the purpose of engaging in prostitution. On appeal, she claimed the ordinance was unconstitutional as void for vagueness, and overbroad. The court agreed. In considering factors whether a person had the intent to engage in, solicit or procure sexual activity for hire, the ordinance listed circumstances which "may" be considered. Since factors other than those enumerated in the statute could be considered, the court agreed the ordinance was impermissibly vague. Further, the ordinance implicated a person's status or otherwise innocent behavior, so was also unconstitutionally overbroad. Therefore, the court vacated the conviction.


OUTCOME: Decision reversed and conviction vacated. Loitering for purposes of prostitution ordinance was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad because factors other than those enumerated could be considered as evidence of intent, and it implicated a person's status or otherwise innocent behavior.

City of Euclid v. Moore


NO. 75143


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 5900



December 9, 1999, Date of Announcement of Decision


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Criminal appeal from the Euclid Municipal Court. Case No. 98-CRB-534 A/B.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Affirmed in part and Reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Euclid Municipal Court (Ohio), which convicted defendant of disrupting school activities and criminal trespass.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was cited for disrupting school activities and trespass in connection with an incident where she accompanied her son to elementary school. Defendant had repeatedly walked her son to his classroom after class had begun. She had been advised by the school and police to adhere to school policies regarding late check-in, including registering with the office and obtaining a visitor's pass. Defendant appealed, arguing the evidence presented at trial was legally insufficient to support her convictions. The court reversed defendant 's conviction for disrupting school activities, construing the applicable city ordinance to prohibit only willful conduct and conduct which either caused the class to terminate in an untimely manner or substantially impaired the conduct of the classroom. There was no evidence defendant's conduct was willful or substantially impaired the lesson. The trespass conviction was affirmed on grounds the jury was free to decide defendant failed to follow established school procedures.


OUTCOME: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part; while jury was free to determine whether defendant's lack of adherence to school policy constituted criminal trespass, the jury had no evidence that defendant's conduct was willful or substantially impaired the conduct of the lesson in her son's classroom.

 

330 of 2888 DOCUMENTS


State v. Michaels


C.A. NO. 18862


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, NINTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, SUMMIT COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 5830



December 8, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM JUDGMENT ENTERED IN THE COURT OF COMMON PLEAS. COUNTY OF SUMMIT, OHIO. CASE NO. CR 94 11 2851.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the Summit County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which adjudicated him a sexual predator.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was adjudicated a sexual predator and appealed. The appellate court affirmed, concluding that because Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950 was remedial rather than punitive, it was not an unconstitutionally retroactive or ex post facto law, and did not violate the double jeopardy clause. The statute was drafted with sufficient precision to provide adequate standards to determine if an individual was a sexual predator. The evidence supported finding, by clear and convincing evidence, that appellant was likely to engage in sexual offenses in the future, considering that victim was a juvenile, and appellant was an adult, appellant drugged victim, and other young men reported similar experiences with appellant; appellant's prior problems with drugs and alcohol; and subsequent intimidation of the victim while out on bond. The statute plainly permitted its application to individuals imprisoned, without qualification of the basis for the incarceration on its effective date.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. The sexual predator statute was not unconstitutionally retroactive, ex post facto, vague, or violative of the double-jeopardy clause. The evidence supported that appellant was likely to engage in sexually oriented offenses in the future. The statute permitted its application to individuals imprisoned on its effective date, regardless of the basis for imprisonment.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Hardin County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), adjudicating him to be a sexual predator pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.09.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that the trial court erred, in violation of the Ex Post Facto Clause of the United States Constitution, in finding appellant to be a sexual predator. Appellant presented no meritorious arguments as to ineffective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed; appellant's contentions that Ohio's sexual predator law was unconstitutional were denied; the statute was designed to protect the public and was not unconstitutionally vague; appellant did not present meritorious arguments as to ineffective assistance of counsel.

State v. Polen


CASE NO. 711


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CARROLL COUNTY

December 8, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Criminal Appeal from Carroll County Common Pleas Court, Case No. 3166.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed an appeal from the decision of the Carroll County Common Pleas Court (Ohio), which found him to be a sexual predator.


OVERVIEW: After appellant was found to have been taking nude pictures of neighborhood children, he pleaded no contest to two counts of illegal use of a minor. He was found to be a sexual predator. The appellate court affirmed. The Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2959.09 (B) (2) factors were sufficient guidelines for a sexual predator determination, and that statute was constitutional. Appellant's claim that he was not informed that he would lose his passport once he pleaded no contest was without merit. It was not required that he be informed about such collateral consequences. Nor was the court required to order a psychological evaluation before determining whether appellant was a sexual predator. Appellant failed to show any particularized need for such an examination. Also, the trial court did not abuse its discretion by denying appellant a continuance. The predator label was supported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: Decision was affirmed. The sexual predator statute contained sufficient guidelines and was constitutional. The trial court was not required to inform appellant about collateral consequences of his plea, nor was it required to authorize a psychological exam. The evidence supported such a status.

State v. Duran


CASE NUMBER 5-99-02


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT, HANCOCK COUNTY


1999-Ohio-948; 1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 5674



December 3, 1999, Date of Judgment Entry


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief granted at, Remanded by State v. Peace, 2012 Ohio 6118, 2012 Ohio App. LEXIS 5284 (Ohio Ct. App., Hancock County, Dec. 26, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Criminal Appeal from Common Pleas Court.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment and sentence of the Hancock County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), following a jury verdict finding him guilty of aggravated murder with one specification, conspiracy to commit aggravated murder, aggravated arson, and tampering with evidence.


OVERVIEW: The court concluded that the trial court's decision to not give a lesser included instruction of murder, when one was given for aggravated murder, was correct, although rendered for an incorrect reason. The evidence presented at trial in the case did not reasonably support an acquittal on aggravated murder and a conviction on the lesser included offense of murder. Accordingly, it was the court's conclusion that there was no error in the failure of the trial court to instruct the jury on the lesser offense of murder. They further held that it was clear that the prosecutor's statements regarding the defendant's silence did not prejudice substantial rights of the defendant, even presuming that they unconstitutionally refer to the defendant's exercise of his Miranda rights, based on the entire record the plaintiff-prosecutor's references were so minor and so oblique as to be harmless beyond any reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed, because the trial court's decision to not give a lesser included instruction of murder, when one was given for aggravated murder, was correct; and the plaintiff-prosecutor's statements regarding the defendant's silence did not prejudice substantial rights of the defendant and were so oblique as to be harmless.

 

336 of 2888 DOCUMENTS


Steele v. Diab


Court of Appeals No. E-98-035


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, ERIE COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 5738



December 3, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Trial Court No. 94-CV-129.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants injured motorist, insurance company, and negligent driver appealed the judgments of the Erie County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which entered a default judgment against appellant insurance company in favor appellant injured motorist, and returned a general verdict in favor of appellee injured party.


OVERVIEW: Appellee sued appellants injured motorist and negligent driver for monetary damages for injuries sustained when plaintiff stopped to assist appellant injured motorist. Appellant injured motorist filed a cross-claim indemnification action against appellant insurance company. The trial court erred in denying appellant injured motorist's motion for set off of the $ 500,000 settlement with appellants negligent driver and insurance company, because appellant insurance company's settlement was not precipitated by their admission of liability, and appellant injured motorist did not have an opportunity to adjudicate appellant negligent driver's liability. The trial court abused its discretion in awarding prejudgment interest to appellee, since the issue of whether appellant injured motorist's negligence was the proximate cause of appellee's injuries was legitimately disputed. Default judgment was improperly entered against appellant insurance company, because the indemnification claim was a new claim and it was served on attorney who had not made an appearance in the case.


OUTCOME: Judgments reversed, because the trial court erred in denying appellant injured motorist's motion for set off, in awarding prejudgment interest to appellee, and in granting default judgment against appellant insurance company since the cross-claim was improperly served.

Later proceeding at State v. Hughbanks, 88 Ohio St. 3d 1459, 726 N.E.2d 502, 2000 Ohio LEXIS 763 (2000)
Motion denied by State v. Hughbanks, 88 Ohio St. 3d 1483, 727 N.E.2d 133, 2000 Ohio LEXIS 928 (2000)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Hughbanks, 2003 Ohio 187, 2003 Ohio App. LEXIS 164 (Ohio Ct. App., Hamilton County, Jan. 17, 2003)

PRIOR HISTORY: Criminal Appeal From: Hamilton County Court of Common Pleas. TRIAL NO. B-9706761.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Appealed From Is: Affirmed. Independent Review: Aggravating Circumstances Outweigh Mitigating Factors. Appropriateness: Sentence of Death is Appropriate.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant criminal defendant challenged a judgment from the Hamilton County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which convicted him of two counts of aggravated murder and the aggravated burglary of his victim's home, and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant criminal defendant was found guilty of two counts of aggravated murder, aggravated burglary, and sentenced him to death. He appealed. Code Ann. § 2929.04(B)(1), (2), or (5) mitigating factors by a preponderance of the evidence. Thus, the trial court did not err in imposing the death sentence. The court concluded that appellant's death sentence was neither excessive nor disproportionate to the death sentence imposed in similar cases in the district.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; appellant's assignments of error had no merit, the aggravating circumstances outweighed mitigating factors, thus the trial court did not err in imposing death sentence, and death sentence was neither excessive nor disproportionate to the death sentence imposed in similar cases in the district.

State v. Fields

COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, HOCKING COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 5744



November 29, 1999, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [*1] JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions for violations of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. §§ 4511.19, 4507.02, 4511.25 and 4573.263 in the Hocking County Municipal Court (Ohio), alleging deprivation of rights under Ohio Const. art. I, § 14 and U.S. Const. amends. IV and XIV when the trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled not guilty to several traffic violations, including driving under the influence of alcohol, Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 4511.19(A)(1), driving under suspension, Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 4507.02, driving left of center line, Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 4511.25), and failing to wear a seat belt, Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 4573.263. IV and XIV or Ohio Const. art. I, § 14.


OUTCOME: The conviction for driving while intoxicated was affirmed when the evidence showed that the police officer possessed the requisite reasonable suspicion to effectuate the traffic stop, and thus was constitutionally permitted.

City of Hamilton v. Johnson


CASE NO. CA99-02-025


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TWELFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, BUTLER COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 5623



November 29, 1999, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [*1] Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant appealed from his conviction in the Hamilton Municipal Court, Butler County (Ohio), for "conduct towards a law enforcement officer" in violation of Hamilton Codified Ordinance 537.16.


OVERVIEW: Two officers impounded a vehicle for expired tags. Appellant himself verified that the tags had expired, then commented loudly and "inappropriately" about the situation. The officers attempted to cite appellant for "conduct towards a law enforcement officer," in violation of Hamilton, Ohio, Codified Ordinance 537.16. Appellant refused to sign the citation and he was arrested. Appellant's motion to dismiss was denied and he was found guilty. Appellant appealed, challenging the ordinance's constitutionality; insufficient evidence to support his conviction; and, entrapment. Affirming appellant's conviction, the court narrowly construed the ordinance to proscribe only "fighting words," finding appellant's words likely to provoke a reasonable person to become involved in an immediate breach of the peace. Appellant's conviction was not against the manifest weight of the evidence; and, since appellant had not established the defense of entrapment during trial, the court refused to consider it on appeal.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed. The ordinance was narrowly construed; proscribing only "fighting words." Appellant's conviction was not against the manifest weight of the evidence; and, since appellant failed to establish entrapment during trial, the court refused to hear it upon appeal.

 

341 of 2888 DOCUMENTS


State v. Darden


C.A. CASE NO. 17395


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, MONTGOMERY COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 5548



November 24, 1999, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] T.C. CASE NO. 97 CR 1523.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant appealed a judgment of the Montgomery County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which found him guilty of possession of crack cocaine in violation of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2925.11(A).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with possession of crack cocaine after being strip searched following a traffic stop. Appellant pled not guilty and filed a motion to suppress arguing that the officers had not possessed reasonable articulable suspicion to make the traffic stop or to pat him down, and that the strip search had been conducted without a warrant in violation of his constitutional rights. After the trial court denied his motion to suppress, appellant was convicted and sentenced. On appeal, the court held that the officers' pat down of appellant was warranted because the totality of the circumstances led the officers to believe that appellant might have been armed and dangerous. The officers were not required to obtain a search warrant to strip search appellant because the search was conducted of appellant's buttocks, and not his body cavity. Thus, strip search of appellant was not unreasonable under U.S. Const. amend. IV.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; pat down of appellant was warranted because totality of circumstances led officers to believe that appellant might have been armed and dangerous. Search warrant to strip search appellant not required because search was conducted of appellant's buttocks, not his body cavity. Strip search of appellant was not unreasonable.

Mayer v. Bristow


CASE NUMBER 3-98-29


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT, CRAWFORD COUNTY


1999-Ohio-933; 1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 5585



November 24, 1999, Date of Judgment Entry


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Civil Appeal from Common Pleas Court.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of Crawford County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), implementing certain restrictions upon his use of the prison mail system; having been declared a "vexatious litigator" after stating that he would file "hundreds and hundreds" of lawsuits against county officials.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had filed numerous lawsuits in different courts directed at various county officials, and was determined by the court to be a vexatious litigator. The trial court issued an order stating that defendant would not have mail privileges at any state institution wherein he may be housed. Defendant sought leave to file a civil rights lawsuit, which was denied, he filed an appeal from the trial court's implementation order. The appellate court held that the procedure established by Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2323.52, the vexatious litigator statute, failed to provide a reasonable and meaningful substitute for direct access to Ohio's trial courts and therefore determined that the statute was unconstitutional in its entirety. The judgment of the Crawford County Court of Common Pleas was reversed.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed, the court holding that the procedure established by Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2323.52, the vexatious litigator statute, failed to provide a reasonable and meaningful substitute for direct access to Ohio's trial courts, determining the statute was unconstitutional.

OVERVIEW: Appellant suffered damage to his teeth when he bit down on a pecan shell baked into one of appellee's cookies. OUTCOME: Affirmed. Presence of pecan shell in pecan cookie was a natural occurrence that appellant reasonably should have anticipated and guarded against. Construing evidence most strongly in favor of appellant, reasonable minds could only conclude that appellee was entitled to summary judgment.

 

344 of 2888 DOCUMENTS


State v. Burkey


CASE NO. 715


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CARROLL COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 5798



November 23, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Criminal Appeal from Carroll County Common Pleas Court, Case No. 3590.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Carroll County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) that adjudicated him a sexual predator, contending Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950 was unconstitutionally vague, levied a second punishment over and above the original sentence imposed, and was an invalid ex post facto law.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was determined to be a sexual predator at hearing held regarding appellant. The court held that Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950 was remedial in nature and did not have a punitive effect. Appellant's contention that a sexual predator determination will lessen the likelihood of parole was speculative. Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.09(B) (1), as applied to conduct prior to the effective date of the statute, did not violate the Ex Post Facto Clause of U.S. Const. art. I § 10. Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.09(D) (2) set forth numerous factors, which clearly provide guidance and minimum standards a trial court must consider in its classification of a defendant as a sexual predator. Ample support was provided in order to conclude by clear and convincing evidence that appellant was a sexual predator. The trial court did not merely rely upon the conviction itself in isolation.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed holding the State established a pattern of activity by appellant against multiple juvenile victims, which were indicative of further sexually oriented offenses. The sexual predator statute was not vague, did not levy a second punishment, and was not an invalid ex post facto law.

State v. Padgett


CASE NO. 97-C.A.-180


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, MAHONING COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 5815



November 23, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Criminal Appeal from Youngstown Municipal Court, Mahoning County, Ohio. Case No. 97 CR 763 A.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State brought this appeal from the Youngstown Municipal Court, Mahoning County (Ohio), which ordered the dismissal of a felony charge against appellee for failure to register as a sexual offender as required by Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.04.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was charged with violating Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.04 for failing to register as a sexual offender. Appellee moved to dismiss, alleging that this statute violated the retroactivity clause of Ohio Const. art. II, § 28, and the ex post facto clause of U.S. Const. art. I, § 10. Appellant State sought review from the grant of appellee's motion, claiming the lower court exceeded its jurisdiction in dismissing the charge and that the sexual offender registration statute did not violate ex post facto prohibitions. Appellee was not allowed to raise, at the preliminary hearing, a motion to dismiss based on the purported unconstitutionality of the statute. The lower court had no jurisdiction to dismiss appellee at preliminary hearing based on that argument. Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950 was neither impermissibly retroactive nor an ex post facto law. Case was reversed and remanded.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded. The lower court was without jurisdiction to dismiss appellee at preliminary hearing, as appellee was not allowed to raise argument that statute was unconstitutional. Previous case law ruled that the sexual offender registration requirement was neither impermissibly retroactive nor an ex post facto law.

State v. Lilly


NO. 74849


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 5454



November 18, 1999, Date of Announcement of Decision


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Criminal appeal from the Court of Common Pleas. Case No. CP-CR-52754.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed judgment of the Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.01 et seq., contending that the requirements of proof beyond a reasonable doubt that he was a sexually violent predator and clear and convincing evidence that he was a sexual predator were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed the determination that he was a sexual predator. Through counsel, defendant charged that Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.01 et seq. was unconstitutional. Thus, there was a rational basis for requiring proof beyond a reasonable doubt that a defendant was a sexually violent predator, and requiring clear and convincing evidence that the defendant was a sexual predator. The court found the registration and notification provisions did not implicate fundamental rights in a manner that would subject the sexual predator law to strict scrutiny.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because there was a rational basis for requiring proof beyond a reasonable doubt that a defendant was a sexually violent predator, and requiring clear and convincing evidence that the defendant was a sexual predator.

State v. Taylor


NO. 75352


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 5455



November 18, 1999, Date of Announcement of Decision


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Amended Nunc Pro Tunc to Correct Page Nine of the Opinion December 16, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Civil appeal from the Court of Common Pleas. Case No. CR-290970.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas, Cuyahoga County (Ohio), which denied his petition for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of aggravated murder with a firearm and sentenced to death. Subsequently, petitioner filed a petition to vacate his sentence pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2953.21. The trial court denied the petition. On appeal, petitioner assigned nine errors for review. Specifically, petitioner contended that his trial and appellate counsel were ineffective and that his conviction was void because the state death penalty statutes were unconstitutional. The court held that petitioner was not denied effective assistance of trial counsel because he did not submit any evidentiary materials to demonstrate the lack of competent counsel or that prejudice resulted therefrom. Petitioner's claim of ineffective assistance of appellate counsel was not cognizable in the postconviction proceeding. Petitioner's constitutional challenge to the death penalty statutes were raised on a prior appeal to the court and, therefore, were barred by the doctrine of res judicata.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; petitioner was not denied effective assistance of trial counsel because he did not submit any evidence to demonstrate lack of competent counsel or that prejudice resulted. Petitioner's ineffective assistance of appellate counsel claim was not cognizable in postconviction proceeding. Petitioner's death penalty challenge was barred by res judicata.

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Board of Zoning Appeals brought an appeal from an order entered by the Summit County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) that remanded this case back to the Board of Zoning Appeals for consideration of appellee's request for an area variance under the correct standard.


OVERVIEW: Trial court remanded a case to appellant Board of Zoning Appeals to consider evidence under the appropriate standard of review. Appellant argued that the trial court should have applied the appropriate standard to the evidence and affirmed the denial of the variance as supported by the preponderance of substantial, reliable, and probative evidence rather than remanding the case. Trial court's actions fell squarely within its jurisdiction. Trial court's finding that appellant applied the incorrect standard of review was supported by substantial, reliable, and probative evidence. Remanding the case to correct this error by applying the appropriate standard of review was not an abuse of discretion. Decision was affirmed.

Crutcher v. Butler Twp.


C.A. Case No. 17775


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, MONTGOMERY COUNTY


135 Ohio App. 3d 582; 735 N.E.2d 25; 1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 5384



November 12, 1999, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] T.C. Case No. 98-899.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from order of the Montgomery County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) granting summary judgment to respondents in appellant's action for workers' compensation benefits due to his alleged mental condition.


OVERVIEW: Appellant commenced an action for workers' compensation benefits, alleging he suffered a mental condition as a result of witnessing a suicide in the course of his employment as a police officer. The lower court granted summary judgment in favor of respondents and appellant appealed. The appellate court affirmed the judgment, concluding the exclusion of compensation for mental stress in the absence of a contemporaneous physical injury in Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 4123.01(C) did not violate the "open courts/right to remedy" provisions of the Ohio constitution as the provision did not foreclose an employee who has suffered a purely psychological injury from pursuing a common law remedy against the employer; the court further concluded the provision did not violate the equal protection clauses of the federal and Ohio Constitutions.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because provision excluding compensation for mental stress absent contemporaneous physical injury did not violate constitutional "open courts/right to remedy" provisions as appellant was not foreclosed from pursuing common law remedy against employer; provision did not violate constitutional equal protection clauses.

 

354 of 2888 DOCUMENTS


Darst v. Bay Village Bd. of Educ.


No. 76091


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 5296



November 10, 1999, Date of Announcement of Decision


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Civil appeal from Court of Common Pleas. Case No. CV-350864.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: APPEAL DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Bay Village Board of Education challenged the judgment of the Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) denying its motion claiming immunity under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2744(C) for injuries to plaintiff while playing a varsity soccer game for her high school.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff cut her knee on an out-of-bounds sprinkler head while playing a varsity soccer game for her high school. She filed this suit seeking compensation from defendant. Both parties filed cross-motions for summary judgment. Plaintiff filed her motion asking for a determination that the board was liable as a matter of law; the board filed its motion claiming immunity under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2744 (C). The court denied both motions. The court held that it lacked jurisdiction to hear the appeal because § 2744.02(C), which authorized an interlocutory appeal by a political subdivision which was denied immunity from suit, was voided by law. Absent statutory authority for the appeal, the order denying the city's motion for summary judgment on sovereign immunity grounds could not be considered a final order and had to therefore be dismissed.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; court held that it lacked jurisdiction to hear the appeal because the section that authorized an interlocutory appeal by a political subdivision which was denied immunity from suit, was voided. Absent statutory authority for the appeal, the order could not be considered a final order and was dismissed.

State v. Ashworth


Case No. 99-CA-60


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LICKING COUNTY

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Civil appeal from the Licking County Court of Common Pleas. Case No. 96-CR-356.

DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant criminal defendant appealed a judgment from the Licking County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which dismissed his petition for post-conviction relief without an evidentiary hearing.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with two counts of aggravated murder, and a separate count of aggravated robbery. Appellant entered a plea of guilty, and waived the presentation of mitigating evidence. A three-judge panel found sufficient basis to find him guilty of aggravated murder, all capital specifications, and aggravated robbery, and sentenced him to death. Appellant appealed the judgment of conviction and sentence to the Ohio Supreme Court, which affirmed, and appellant filed a petition for post-conviction relief, arguing primarily that counsel was ineffective for failing to present mitigating evidence. State v. Anderson


C.A. Case No. 98-CA-44


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, MIAMI COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 5182



November 5, 1999, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] T.C. Case No. 90-CR-56.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order classifying him as a sexual predator, pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed an order classifying him as a sexual predator, pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950. The appellate court concluded that the statute was not violative of constitutional prohibitions against cruel and unusual punishment, double jeopardy, impermissibly vague laws, or ex post facto laws. The court reversed and remanded, however, concluding that pursuant to its decision in White, the provision requiring a trial judge to consider certain factors in making the finding of fact whether a sexual offender was likely to re-offend, Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950(B)(2), was unconstitutional as it encroached upon the judicial power in violation of the separation of powers under the Ohio Constitution. The court determined that, on remand, the lower court must redetermine whether defendant was a sexual predator without the requirement of considering any of the factors set forth in the statute.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded because mandated consideration of factors pursuant to statute was unconstitutional as it imposed upon judicial branch the legislature's determination of what evidence was relevant to factual determination; remanded for redetermination whether defendant was sexual predator without requiring consideration of such factors.

State v. Elliott


C.A. Case No. 98-CA-36


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, MIAMI COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 5191



November 5, 1999, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] T.C. Case No. 83-CR-83.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of trial court Reversed, and cause Remanded for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant appealed from an order of the trial court (Ohio) that classified him as a sexual predator after he was convicted of three counts of attempted rape, and was sentenced to three concurrent terms of five to 15 years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant appealed from an order classifying him as a sexual predator, pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. ch. 2950. On appeal, appellant argued that the statute violated prohibitions against cruel and unusual punishment, double jeopardy, impermissibly vague laws, and ex post facto laws of the U.S. or Ohio constitutions. The court held the statute did not violate those constitutional provisions. Thus, defense counsel did not provide ineffective assistance of counsel by not raising those arguments at the hearing held to determine appellant's sexual predator status. The provision in Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.09(B)(2) requiring a trial judge to consider certain factors in making the finding of fact whether a sexual offender was likely to re-offend encroached upon the judicial power in violation of the separation of powers implicit in the Ohio Constitution. The judgment was reversed.


OUTCOME: Judgment of trial court reversed and remanded. Sexual predator statute provision requiring judge to consider factors in making finding whether sexual offender was likely to re-offend encroached on judge's power in violation of separation of powers in constitution.

State v. White


C.A. Case No. 98-CA-37


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, MIAMI COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 5193



November 5, 1999, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] T.C. Case No. 78-CR-146.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment determining him to be a sexual predator pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.


OVERVIEW: The court concluded that Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950 does not violate prohibitions against cruel and unusual punishment or double jeopardy of the United States and Ohio Constitutions, nor the prohibition against ex post facto laws of the United States Constitution, because it is not a punishment, but rather designed to ensure public safety; the factors of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.09(B)(2) are not impermissibly vague in violation of the Due Process Clauses of the United States or Ohio Constitutions; that Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950 does not constitute an unreasonable exercise of the police power and does not deny convicted sex offenders the equal protection of the law; and that the statute impermissibly encroached upon the judicial power, by prescribing factors that a trial court was required to consider in making a finding of fact. Accordingly, the court declared that aspect of the statute to be unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded; the court found Ohio's sexual predator law unconstitutional because it prescribes factors that the trial court was required to consider in making a finding of fact, and thus the court declared that aspect of the statute to be unconstitutional.

State v. Spade


C.A. Case No. 98-CA-40


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, MIAMI COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 5199



November 5, 1999, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] T.C. Case No. 96-CR-70.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant appealed the order of the Miami County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) classifying him as a sexual predator, pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.


OVERVIEW: Appellant appealed the order classifying him as a sexual predator, pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950 (statute). The statute did not violate the prohibitions against cruel and unusual punishment, double jeopardy or ex post facto laws contained in the Ohio or United States constitutions. The factors in the statute were not impermissibly vague and were not an unreasonable exercise of the police power, nor a denial of equal protection of the law. Appellant did not receive ineffective assistance of counsel. The purpose of the statute could be accomplished without mandating that trial courts consider certain factors in making the requisite finding of fact. The mandated consideration of factors was unconstitutional, and the trial court had to redetermine whether appellant was a sexual predator, as defined by Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.01(E), without being required to consider any of the factors.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded; trial court had to redetermine whether appellant was a sexual predator, as defined by the statute, without being required to consider any of the factors set forth in the statute, as the mandated consideration of factors was unconstitutional.

State v. Norris

COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, MONTGOMERY COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 5206



November 5, 1999, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] T.C. CASE NO. 98 CR 2392.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Montgomery County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which denied his motion to suppress evidence and convicted him for possession of non-crack cocaine.


OVERVIEW: The victim signed a domestic violence statement against defendant and told the officer that he might find defendant staying at a motel. The officer proceeded to the motel and, after locating defendant's van in the parking lot, called for back-up. After back-up arrived the officers went to defendant's motel room and knocked. Defendant opened the door, stayed inside the room and did not invite the officers to enter. The officers entered the motel room, arrested defendant and found cocaine in his pocket. Defendant filed a motion to suppress the evidence, which was denied, and defendant was convicted. On appeal the court reversed the conviction and remanded because defendant had a reasonable expectation of privacy in a motel room, and the state could not claim hot pursuit where a police officer delayed making an arrest for the purpose of obtaining back-up assistance from other officers.


OUTCOME: Conviction reversed and remanded because defendant had a reasonable expectation of privacy in a motel room, and the state could not claim hot pursuit where a police officer delayed making an arrest for the purpose of obtaining back-up assistance from other officers.

State v. Hubbard


CASE NO. 97-T-0144


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, TRUMBULL COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 5248



November 5, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Discretionary appeal not allowed by State v. Hubbard, 88 Ohio St. 3d 1437, 724 N.E.2d 812, 2000 Ohio LEXIS 710 (2000)
