PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Criminal Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 91 CR 431.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant appealed the judgment of the Trumbull County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) denying his request for a transfer to a different psychiatric hospital.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with murder and attempted murder and was incompetent to stand trial. The trial court determined that appellant's commitment at the psychiatric center was the least restrictive alternative available consistent with public safety and appellant's treatment goals. The trial court rejected appellant's request to be transferred to a different hospital. Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2945.401(G)(2) required the state to prove, by clear and convincing evidence, the threat to public safety from a recommended change in conditions of commitment. Appellee state failed to meet its burden of establishing that appellant's proposed transfer represented a threat to public safety. Appellee failed to present any evidence as to the less-secure hospital's inability to properly house insanity acquittees such as appellant. The trial court abused its discretion in rejecting a doctor's opinion, without any contrary evidence, that appellant's transfer to a civil mental hospital was the least restrictive commitment.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded; appellee state failed to meet its burden of establishing that appellant's proposed transfer represented a threat to public safety, no evidence was presented as to the hospital's inability to properly house insanity acquittees such as appellant.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State appealed from an order of the Court of Common Pleas, Cuyahoga County (Ohio), which granted appellee's motion to suppress evidence based upon an unlawful arrest.


OVERVIEW: Police officers stopped appellee for driving through a stop sign. Although appellee did not have his driver's license, he offered a receipt from the municipal court holding his license as proof that he had a valid driver's license. The officers arrested appellee; searched his car; and, found evidence of drug possession. State v. Tomko


C.A. NO. 19253


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, NINTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, SUMMIT COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 5133



November 3, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM JUDGMENT ENTERED IN THE AKRON MUNICIPAL COURT. COUNTY OF SUMMIT, OHIO. CASE NO. 97TRC27827.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence for driving with a prohibited breath-alcohol content in violation of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 4511.19(A)(3) from the Akron Municipal Court, Summit County (Ohio).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was caught speeding, and when he was pulled over, the officer noticed a mild odor of alcohol. The officer administered the Horizontal Gaze Nystagmus test and field sobriety test, both of which the defendant performed poorly. Defendant also submitted to a breath test that he failed. Defendant was convicted and sentenced for driving with a prohibited breath-alcohol content in violation of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 4511.19(A)(3), and he appealed. The court determined the combination of defendant's bloodshot eyes, a smell of alcohol, and his admission that he had consumed two beers was sufficient to provide the officer with reasonable suspicion to detain the defendant. The above factors, coupled with poor performance of administered tests, provided probable cause to arrest defendant. The court determined that the breath test was properly administered by the office, the results were accurate, and the admission of the results was proper.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; defendant's bloodshot eyes, a smell of alcohol, failure of field tests, and admission he had consumed two beers was sufficient to provide officer with reasonable suspicion to detain defendant; breath test was properly administered.

State v. Henize


CASE NO. CA99-04-008


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TWELFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, BROWN COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 5123



November 1, 1999, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [*1] Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant appealed his conviction by the Brown County Court (Ohio) for aggravated menacing in violation of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2903.21(A).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated menacing after threatening four juvenile boys with a gun. Appellant challenged, alleging there was insufficient evidence to support the verdict and the conviction was contrary to the manifest weight of the evidence. Further, appellant claimed prejudice when prosecution was allowed to change identity of one of the victims, by not being allowed to confront a witness in violation of U.S. Const., amend. OUTCOME: Affirmed; the evidence supported the belief appellant would cause serious physical harm. The offense was proven beyond a reasonable doubt and not against the manifest weight of the evidence. Amending the complaint was not prejudicial as the victim's name was not essential. Appellant's legal counsel was neither unreasonable nor prejudicial.

Bailey v. Republic Engineered Steels, Inc.


Case No. 1999CA00084


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, STARK COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 5162



November 1, 1999, Date of Judgment Entry


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Appeal from the Stark County Court of Common Pleas. Case No. 98CV02308.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal by appellant of judgment of the Stark County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) dismissing appellant's complaint in workers' compensation case in which appellant suffered from depression after accidentally running over a coworker, who was killed as a result.


OVERVIEW: While operating a tow motor at appellee's facility, appellant accidentally ran over a coworker, who was killed as a result. Appellant suffered from and received treatment for psychological and psychiatric conditions, including depression following the accident. Appellant sought to participate in the Workers' Compensation Fund, but trial court granted appellee's motion to dismiss appellant's complaint, finding purely psychiatric conditions were not included within the definition of "injury" under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 4123.01(C)(1) and that appellant did not have a compensable injury under the Workers' Compensation Act. The court reversed, finding that the psychiatric condition alleged in appellant's complaint arising from an injury to his co-worker was a compensable injury within the meaning of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 4123.01(C)(1). The court was required to give the statute such a construction in order to preserve its constitutional validity.


OUTCOME: Judgment dismissing appellant's complaint reversed; psychiatric condition alleged in appellant's complaint arising from injury to his co-worker was a compensable injury under Workers' Compensation Act.

 

368 of 2888 DOCUMENTS


Penn Traffic Co. v. Clark County Bd. of Elections


C.A. Case No. 99-CA-26


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, CLARK COUNTY


138 Ohio App. 3d 1; 740 N.E.2d 290; 1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 5077



October 29, 1999, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected April 19, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: T.C. Case No. 98-CV-0878.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervenor appellant, shopping center, sought review from a judgment of the Clark County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) dismissing its intervening complaint by contending that it was denied due process of law when it was not notified of a pending local option election related to the sale of liquor.


OVERVIEW: Intervenor shopping center was the landlord for plaintiff store, which lost its liquor license in a local option election. Since a local option election was a legislative action, intervenors enjoyed no constitutional due process right to notice of the election. Because a liquor permit holder had no constitutional due process right to notice of a local liquor election, perforce the permit holder's landlord had no right either. The court found that the remedy for the correction of all defect in an election was not to void the election, but rather to contest the election. Intervenor failed to file an election contest within the appropriate time or pursue the remedy available to it, and regardless of the alleged impropriety of the election, was precluded from pursuing any other action to overturn its result.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed holding that intervenors had no constitutional due process, or statutory, right to notification of local option elections and since it failed to pursue its remedy, regardless of the alleged impropriety of the election, it was precluded from pursuing any other action to overturn its result.

Donsante v. City of Wickliffe


CASE NOS. 98-L-046 and 98-L-047


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LAKE COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 5098



October 29, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Dismissed by, Discretionary appeal not allowed by Donsante v. Wickliffe, 88 Ohio St. 3d 1412, 723 N.E.2d 118, 2000 Ohio LEXIS 264 (2000)
Related proceeding at Foster v. City of Wickliffe, 2007 Ohio 7132, 2007 Ohio App. LEXIS 6241 (Ohio Ct. App., Lake County, Dec. 31, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Civil Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas. Case nos. 94 CV 000102 and 94 CV 000103.

This Opinion Substituted by the Court for Vacated Opinion of September 30, 1999, Previously Reported at: 1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 4643.
Donsante v. City of Wickliffe, 1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 4643 (Ohio Ct. App., Lake County, Sept. 30, 1999)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Reversed and judgment entered for appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged a Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) judgment that upheld an ordinance enacted by appellee to regulate the parking of recreational vehicles in front yards of residential districts.


OVERVIEW: In the consolidated cases of appellants (two couples), appellants challenged the judgment of the county court which upheld an ordinance enacted by appellee (the City of Wickliffe) to regulate the parking of recreational vehicles in the front yards of residential districts. On appeal, the appellate court reversed. Because appellee failed to provide notice to owners of boats, boat trailers, and vehicles exceeding three- quarter ton rating capacity, appellee deprived appellants and the city of a full public hearing. Appellee did not complete the proper steps in order to enact the ordinance. Before it could adopt the ordinance, appellee was required to submit it to the voters. Since it did not, the ordinance was not properly enacted. Because appellants' third, fourth, and fifth assignments of error were moot, the court did not rule on the constitutionality of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: Reversed and judgment entered for appellants. Because appellee failed to provide proper notice to allow parties to make objections to ordinance before passing it, appellants were deprived of a full public hearing and ordinance was not properly enacted.

 

371 of 2888 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lathan


CASE NO. CA98-09-191


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TWELFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, BUTLER COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 4959



October 25, 1999, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [*1] Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part, and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed the Hamilton Municipal Court's (Ohio) decisions which overruled his motion to suppress evidence and imposed a fine and imprisonment for his convictions of obstructing official business, drug abuse, and possession of drug paraphernalia.


OVERVIEW: When appellant was stopped, he told the officer that he did not have his license and spun around to keep the officer from completing the pat-down search. Appellant was arrested, and the officer began an inventory search of the vehicle: marijuana, rolling papers, and appellant's license were found within the passenger compartment and on his person. Appellant's motion to suppress and/or dismiss, arguing that the police lacked probable cause, was overruled. Appellant was found guilty of obstructing official business, drug abuse, and possession of drug paraphernalia, sentenced to jail and imposition of fines. On appeal, substantial evidence supported the obstruction arrest, so the searches were lawful; therefore, the suppression motion was properly denied. Although the record was silent as to statutory criteria, the court presumed the lower court acted properly regarding the imposition of jail time; however, it abused its discretion by not making findings regarding the ability to pay fines.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed regarding motion to suppress, as substantial evidence supported decision; affirmed as to imposition of jail time because court presumed correct; reversed and remanded for findings to support the imposition of both a prison term and a fine, and regarding appellant's ability to pay, because of silent record below.

 

372 of 2888 DOCUMENTS


State v. Taylor


CASE NOS. CA99-05-042, CA99-05-043


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TWELFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CLERMONT COUNTY


135 Ohio App. 3d 182; 733 N.E.2d 310; 1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 4962



October 25, 1999, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state of Ohio, appealed the decision of the Clermont County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) which granted the motion to suppress made by defendants concerning the knock and announce rule under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2935.12.


OVERVIEW: Police knocked on defendants' door, and after pausing approximately three to four seconds, forcibly entered the residence. Once inside the residence, the police searched it and found $ 560 in currency, two digital scales, a grow light, ten bags of marijuana and seven firearms. Defendants were indicted on marijuana possession and distribution charges. Defendants filed a motion to suppress all of the evidence the police gathered, and argued the search violated the Ohio knock and announce statute, Ohio Rev. Code ann. § 2935.12 and the U.S. Const. amend. IV. The court determined the defendants did not have a full and fair warning before the police entered their house. Defendants were given three to four seconds, which, absent exigent circumstances, was not a reasonable opportunity for the residents to open the door of their own volition. Marijuana was not gathered from a source independent of the constitutional violation, thus it should have been suppressed.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; police waiting only three to four seconds before forcibly entering house absent exigent circumstances, was not a reasonable opportunity for defendants to open the door of their own volition under the knock and announce rule during a search.

Gertsma v. City of Berea


No. 74063


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


135 Ohio App. 3d 655; 735 N.E.2d 459; 1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 4914



October 21, 1999, Date of Announcement of Decision


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Civil appeal from Court of Common Pleas. Case No. CV-303786.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed a grant of summary judgment for defendant city by the Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) in plaintiffs' declaratory judgment action challenging the constitutionality of Berea, Ohio, Codified Ordinance No. 90-117, which required owners of certain apartment buildings to arrange for private trash collection.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, landlords of eight-unit apartment buildings, brought a declaratory judgment action against defendant city, challenging the constitutionality of Berea, Ohio, Codified Ordinance No. 90-117. That ordinance required owners of commercial buildings and apartment buildings with more than four units to arrange and pay for private trash collection. The city provided trash collection for other residential buildings, including condominiums with more than four units. Plaintiffs claimed the ordinance violated their rights to equal protection under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ohio Const. art. I, § 2. The trial court granted defendant's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court found the city's desire to cut the costs of garbage collection was a sufficient basis for distinguishing between apartments with more than four units and condominiums with more than four units. Affidavits challenged by plaintiffs did not affect the court's decision and in any event were sufficiently based on personal knowledge.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment for defendant city affirmed, because defendant had an economic basis for distinguishing between apartment buildings with more than four units and other residential buildings in providing trash collection.

Malcolm-Smith v. Goff


NO. 74648


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 4915



October 21, 1999, Date of Announcement of Decision


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected November 1, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Civil appeal from the Court of Common Pleas. Case No. CV-342589.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from judgment of the Cuyahoga County Common Pleas Court (Ohio), granting judgment on the pleadings in favor of defendants state superintendent of public education, the state, and the governor in a case brought by parents and citizens challenging the constitutionality of a state law creating a "municipal school district."


OVERVIEW: A group of parents and citizens alleged that a state law that created a "municipal school district," pursuant to a federal desegregation order, violated several provisions of the Ohio Constitution. The court first determined that a previous federal order in the matter did not preclude the instant action, because plaintiffs-appellants were not in privity with plaintiffs in the federal claim. The court agreed with plaintiffs-appellants that the four-year delay preceding the referendum was unduly long, but then determined that the legislature should cure the problem by revising the question submitted pursuant to the referendum election. The court then held that nothing in either the state or federal Constitution conflicted with the Cleveland mayor's responsibility under the law to appoint board members, nor did the law unconstitutionally confer corporate powers upon the mayor. The law was of a general nature and could potentially apply to any school district.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed, because nothing in either the state or federal Constitution conflicted with the Cleveland mayor's responsibility under the law to appoint board members, nor did the law unconstitutionally confer corporate powers upon the mayor.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant criminal defendant appealed an order from the Belmont County Common Pleas Court (Ohio), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief without an evidentiary hearing.


OVERVIEW: Appellant criminal defendant appealed the decision of the trial court that denied his petition for post-conviction relief without an evidentiary hearing. OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; appellant's 42 claims of error, mostly concerning constitutionality of death penalty scheme, were without merit, and many others were summarily dismissed without a hearing on basis of res judicata, or were meritless.

Haynes v. City of Franklin


CASE NO. CA99-02-023


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TWELFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, WARREN COUNTY


135 Ohio App. 3d 82; 732 N.E.2d 1060; 1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 4865



October 18, 1999, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant appealed an order of the Warren County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) overruling appellant's motion for summary judgment on appellees' claim that appellant violated Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2744.02 requiring it to keep its roads free of nuisance and recovery for appellees' damages and injuries.


OVERVIEW: Appellee husband was driving a semi-trailer when a tire went off the roadway because of a severe drop-off. Appellee husband was seriously injured. The complaint alleged that appellant was negligent in resurfacing the road and had violated Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2744.02 which required it to keep its roads free of nuisance. Appellant filed a motion for summary judgment stating it was immune from liability. The trial court's order clearly affected a substantial right because it denied appellant's statutory immunity defense, but it could revise the order; therefore, it remained an interlocutory and not appealable order. The order was not entered into after a special proceeding defined as Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2505.02(A)(2) because loss of consortium and an action for personal injuries caused by another's negligence were recognized at common law and therefore were not special proceedings. The trial court's order was not a final, appealable order.


OUTCOME: Appeal dismissed; trial court's order was not final or appealable because denial of summary judgment did not constitute a final order, unless the underlying actions were special proceedings. Loss of consortium and personal injury action caused by another's negligence were recognized at common law and, therefore, were not special proceedings.

 

380 of 2888 DOCUMENTS


Sellers v. State


CASE NO. 99-T-0117


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, TRUMBULL COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 4861



October 15, 1999, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [*1] JUDGMENT: Petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed writ of habeas corpus seeking his immediate release from a state prison.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner's habeas corpus petition claimed he was entitled to be released immediately because the procedure for the imposition of post-release control was unconstitutional. The court determined the petition named the State of Ohio as the sole respondent. Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2725.04(B) provided that an application for a writ of habeas corpus must state the name of the person who was responsible for petitioner's confinement. The proper respondent in most habeas corpus actions was the jailer or warden of the penitentiary in which petitioner was detained. Accordingly, the sole respondent in this matter should have been the warden of the specific institution where petitioner was detained. As petitioner did not name that person as a party and did not try to serve the petition upon him, he failed to comply with the requirements of § 2725.04(B) and his petition failed.


OUTCOME: Habeas corpus petition dismissed; proper respondent in habeas corpus action was the jailer or warden of the penitentiary in which petitioner was detained; petitioner did not name that person as a party, thus his petition failed.

State v. Jordan


CASE NO. 97-T-0088


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, TRUMBULL COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 4873



October 15, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief dismissed at State v. Jordan, 2007 Ohio 1067, 2007 Ohio App. LEXIS 1000 (Ohio Ct. App., Trumbull County, Mar. 9, 2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Jordan, 2015-Ohio-1223, 2015 Ohio App. LEXIS 1251 (Ohio Ct. App., Trumbull County, Mar. 31, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Criminal Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas. Case No. 96 CR 269.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant appealed from Trumbull County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) that entered conviction and sentence for kidnapping and aggravated robbery. Trial court overruled appellant's motions to suppress evidence, to waive speedy trial, and to change venue, but granted his motion to dismiss one count.


OVERVIEW: Appellant appealed from his conviction and sentence for kidnapping, aggravated robbery, and control of a firearm. On appeal, the court affirmed. State v. Bradley

DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Common Pleas Court of Logan County (Ohio) adjudicating him a sexual predator pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of rape and, pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.09(B)(2), the trial court determined that appellant was a sexual predator. State v. Britton


Court of Appeals No. L-99-1129


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LUCAS COUNTY


135 Ohio App. 3d 151; 733 N.E.2d 288; 1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 4777



October 8, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected November 20, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Trial Court No. CR98-2543.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant car owner appealed a judgment of the Lucas County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio), which found that appellant was responsible for the towing and storage expenses incurred as the result of the seizure of her motor vehicle by the police.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's boyfriend was arrested and charged with the offenses of rape, kidnapping, and possession of crack cocaine. The victim of the alleged rape and kidnapping claimed that the boyfriend was driving appellant's car at the time, and the police seized the car. Most of the charges were dismissed, and appellant filed a motion for release of her vehicle, which was granted. Appellant was ordered to pay towing and storage charges, and she appealed. The court held that because the criminal charges related to the use of the lawfully seized motor vehicle were dismissed, and the person entitled to possession of the vehicle was an innocent third party, that person was not liable for the expenses of towing and storage of the motor vehicle. The law enforcement agency that seized the property was required to return the property at the earliest possible time pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2933.41(B).


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; liability for towing and storage expenses were a matter between the police and the third party towing and storage company with whom it contracted to provide those services.

Therefore, the case was remanded for resentencing.


OUTCOME: Convictions affirmed but remanded for resentencing; there was no manifest miscarriage of justice by the jury in convicting defendant and jury was properly instructed on evidence; there was error by the trial court in merging the convictions of rape and kidnapping.

OVERVIEW: Appellant was indicted for driving under the influence of alcohol under both Ohio Rev. Code 4511.19(A)(1) and Ohio Rev. Code 4511.19(A)(3). State v. Elms


C.A. NO. 97CA006978


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, NINTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LORAIN COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 4719



October 6, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM JUDGMENT ENTERED IN THE COURT OF COMMON PLEAS, COUNTY OF LORAIN, OHIO. CASE NO. 97CR050112.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a conviction by the Lorain County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) for aggravated trafficking in drugs.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for aggravated trafficking in drugs. The defendant alleged improper hearsay and irrelevant testimony was admitted at trial. The court determined the evidence which related to the search of defendant's home five days prior to the sale of crack was admissible because it met the requirements of Ohio R. Evid. 404(B) because it was not offered to show conformity with previous bad acts in order to besmirch the defendant's character. Rather, it was offered to show preparation or plan. Evidence of the witness' testimony in response to a question by defense counsel regarding whether defendant was a target of the police department was not hearsay because it was offered to explain why the department pursued the investigation into defendant's involvement in drug trafficking. Defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel because his counsel had no duty to withdraw and testify on defendant's behalf.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; evidence admissible because it was used to show preparation or plan and not conformity with previous bad acts; not hearsay because not offered to prove truth of the matter asserted; counsel had no duty to withdraw and testify on defendant's behalf.

Wilde v. Ohio Veterinary Med. Licensing Bd.


Case No. 98CA00138, 98CA00025


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LICKING COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 4813



October 1, 1999, Date of Judgment Entry


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Appeal from the Licking County Court of Common Pleas. Case No. 98CV665.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant veterinarian appealed two judgment entries from the Licking County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) that affirmed the appellee Ohio Veterinary Medical Licensing Board's decision to revoke appellant's license and granted appellee's motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: After a three-day hearing the appellee Ohio Veterinary Medical Licensing Board revoked appellant's veterinary license. The court ruled that the board had inherent authority to reconsider their own decisions until the actual institution of a court appeal, thus they had no jurisdiction to reopen appellant's case at the administrative level, and the trial court did not err in granting appellee's motion to dismiss. The court found the trial court's decision supported by reliable, probative, and substantial evidence; and the order was in accordance of law. Since appellant failed to object to any potential due process violations before the hearing examiner or before the board, this argument was waived on appeal.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because trial court's decision was supported by reliable, probative, and substantial evidence; and the order was in accordance of law; motion to dismiss proper since administrative agency lacked authority to reconsider once court appeal had begun.

 

391 of 2888 DOCUMENTS


Gilmore v. American Community Mut. Ins. Co.


Court of Appeals No. L-99-1064


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LUCAS COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 4565



September 30, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Trial Court No. CI98-1990.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Lucas County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) denying her motion for summary judgment and granting the motion for summary judgment filed by appellee insurer in appellant's suit alleging breach of contract and lack of good faith.


OVERVIEW: Appellant had medical insurance coverage with appellee insurer when she gave birth to her daughter. The daughter was injured during the cesarean delivery and suffered a skull depression. Appellee was sent a hospital bill associated with the child's medical care and treatment. Appellee refused to pay the child's medical expenses because its policy required that in order for a newborn child to be automatically insured, more than one family member had to be insured under the policy when the birth occurred. Appellant was a single mother. Thereafter, appellant sued, alleging breach of contract and lack of good faith. The trial court granted appellee summary judgment. On appeal, appellant argued that appellee's policy was unconstitutional because it treated babies born to single mothers differently than babies born to married mothers. The court affirmed, holding that while children of single mothers could be affected, appellee's policy did not exclude coverage to this group alone.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. Appellee insurer's medical insurance policy and the former statute were not unconstitutional because all newborns who were similarly situated would have been treated the same, regardless of the mother's marital status.

State v. Gilliam


C.A. CASE No. 17491


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, MONTGOMERY COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 4574



September 30, 1999, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] T.C. CASE NO. 98 CR 1930.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant appealed his convictions for rape, kidnapping and possession of cocaine on grounds that the trial court erred by refusing to give jury instruction, attorney's conduct constituted ineffective assistance, and convictions were unsupported by sufficient evidence and against the manifest weight of the evidence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of rape, kidnapping and possession of cocaine. He appealed his convictions, arguing the trial court erred by denying and by refusing jury, attorney's conduct constituted ineffective assistance, and convictions were unsupported by sufficient evidence and against the manifest weight of the evidence. The convictions were affirmed. Motion for acquittal was properly denied. Request for jury instruction on affirmative defense of consent was properly refused because consent is not an affirmative defense to the charge of rape. Attorney's conduct was not deficient nor was it shown to be prejudicial, and convictions were not against manifest weight of evidence.


OUTCOME: Convictions affirmed; lower court did not err by denying motion for acquittal or by refusing jury instruction on affirmative defense of consent, attorney's conduct did not constitute ineffective assistance, and convictions were neither unsupported by sufficient evidence nor against the manifest weight of the evidence.

Gladieux v. Ohio State Med. Bd.


No. 98AP-1296


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


133 Ohio App. 3d 465; 728 N.E.2d 459; 1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 4608



September 30, 1999, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant appealed the order of the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) affirming the appellee state medical board's disciplinary action against appellant doctor regarding his license to practice medicine.


OVERVIEW: Appellee state medical board alleged that appellant physician's sexual relationships with patients' parents violated minimal standards of care pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 4731.22(B)(6). Appellee issued an order suspending appellant's license to practice medicine. Appellant's experts testified that sexual relationships with a parent was inadvisable and not recommended. The evidence provided that the ethical principles, although broadly written, provided sufficient notice that the conduct was prohibited. The board was well within its statutory authority and had the discretion to weigh the evidence and determine that the physician had violated the ethics code. The board's finding of a potential effect on patient care did not violate appellant's constitutional rights. The board had reliable, probative and substantial evidence to find that appellant's care fell below the minimal standards of care of the profession. There was reliable, probative, and substantial evidence to support the board's findings.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; appellant physician's sexual relationships with patients' parents violated minimal standards of care pursuant to statutory provisions; appellee medical board was well within its authority to discipline appellant.

 

394 of 2888 DOCUMENTS


State v. Myers


No. 98AP-1448


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, TENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, FRANKLIN COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 4619



September 30, 1999, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Myers, 2012 Ohio 2733, 2012 Ohio App. LEXIS 2397 (Ohio Ct. App., Franklin County, June 19, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Franklin County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) finding him guilty of three counts of rape, each with a sexually violent predator specification, two counts of aggravated burglary, one count of burglary and one count of kidnapping with a sexual motivation specification.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of rape, aggravated burglary, and kidnapping. On appeal, the court held that a nurse's hearsay statements did not bear on any cognizable diagnosis or treatment and did not fall under Fed. R. Evid. 803(4). However, a doctor's testimony that was pertinent to an accurate diagnosis was admissible. The victim's initial, spontaneous relation that she had been attacked qualified as an excited utterance, but statements made after the stress of the attack lost its domination over the woman's reflective faculties were not admissible. Defendant's claim that his convictions were not supported by sufficient evidence was unpersuasive. Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2971.01(H)(2) was reasonably clear and provided sufficient guidance to the jury to determine whether a defendant was likely to commit a sexually violent offense in the future, but the evidence was insufficient to find beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was a sexually violent predator.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part, case remanded; certain hearsay statements made were not admissible in court and plaintiff was erroneously classified as a sexually violent offender, but defendant's convictions for kidnapping and rape were not against the manifest weight of the evidence.

Junction 615, Inc. v. Liquor Control Comm'n


CASE NOS. 98-L-121 and 98-L-123


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LAKE COUNTY


135 Ohio App. 3d 33; 732 N.E.2d 1025; 1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 4646



September 30, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Administrative Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas. Case Nos. 97 CV 002435 and 98 CV 000081.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant gentlemen's club appealed the Lake County Court of Common Pleas' (Ohio) judgment which denied its administrative appeal from the ruling of appellee Liquor Control Commission.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employed dancers who performed sophisticated dance routines for the patrons. Twice, the appellee liquor commission sent agents to appellant's establishment to determine whether the routines were in violation of the former version of Ohio Adm. Code § 4301:1-1-52 (Rule 52), which prohibited lewd, immoral activities and improper conduct in liquor establishments. The court determined that appellant's conduct was not protected by U.S. Const. amend. I. The court determined that appellant's overbroad challenge was moot. However, the vagueness challenge to Rule 52 had merit because the regulation mentioned no standards whatsoever to guide one in determining what would constitute a violation. The agents were left to decide, with unlimited discretion, what violated the regulation. Furthermore, nothing in the regulation spelled out that contact between dancers and patrons was prohibited by Rule 52, it appeared that it was the agents who determined that it was prohibited. A regulation giving agents such limitless discretion was improper.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded; vagueness challenge to regulation had merit because it mentioned no standards whatsoever to guide one in determining what would constitute a violation.

397 of 2888 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kutnar


CASE NO. 98-L-117


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, ELEVENTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, LAKE COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 4652



September 30, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDINGS: Criminal Appeal from the Court of Common Pleas, Case No. 97 CR 000361.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant appealed the judgment of the Lake County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) which convicted him of abduction and domestic violence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of abduction and domestic violence, and was ordered to serve concurrent prison terms. A jury instruction on a lesser offense was not warranted because the jury could not have reasonably acquitted appellant of abduction, while convicting him only of unlawful restraint. Appellee state introduced overwhelming and substantially uncontroverted evidence that appellant used actual force on the victim. The jury could not have reasonably acquitted appellant of domestic violence, while convicting him only of the misdemeanor of disorderly conduct. The defense did present evidence that the victim had voluntarily gone with appellant; appellant was barred from mentioning that he wanted to go for an AIDS test because the victim had told him about her work as an escort. Appellant was not deprived of his constitutional right to confront an adverse witness simply because the trial court barred any inquiry into the victim's alleged work as an escort.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; appellant did not present evidence to show that he was prejudiced by a failure of the trial court to consider lesser-included offenses, he was not denied due process and his sentence was not unlawful.

State v. Gregory


NO. 74859


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 4670



September 30, 1999, Date of Announcement of Decision


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: Criminal appeal from Common Pleas Court Case No. CR-283264.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Cuyahoga County Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) determining that defendant was a sexual predator pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950 et seq. subject to all attendant registration requirements.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of sexual battery and found to be a sexual predator. The procedural requirements of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.09(B) were satisfied because both plaintiff state as well as defendant were afforded the opportunity to present their respective positions, and counsel represented defendant at the time of the hearing. Plaintiff failed to provide any evidence beyond the bare facts of defendant's conviction of the determination regarding the likelihood of future offenses. The sexual battery conviction alone was insufficient to support the sexual predator determination. The conviction was based primarily upon a plea of guilty where no testimony was offered or evidence submitted regarding the facts of the underlying offense. Defendant fell into that classification of sexual offenders under Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.09(C)(1); there was no error in conducting the sexual predator hearing to determine whether defendant should be adjudicated a sexual predator.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part; statutory procedural requirements were satisfied but there was no show of clear and convincing evidence that defendant was more likely than not predisposed to commit another sexually oriented offense.

State v. Johnson


NO. 74841


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, EIGHTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, CUYAHOGA COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 4678



September 30, 1999, Date of Announcement of Decision


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CHARACTER OF PROCEEDING: CRIMINAL APPEALS FROM COURT OF COMMON PLEAS. CASE NO. CR-176131.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant appealed from the order of the Court of Common Pleas (Ohio) which determined that he was a sexual predator pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.01 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellant had been serving a prison sentence for aggravated burglary and gross sexual imposition since the early 1980's. On June 3, 1998, the trial court conducted a sexual predator determination hearing, and found appellant to be a sexual predator pursuant to Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2950.01 et seq. During the hearing, the trial court was merely presented with the prosecutor's recitation of the fact of appellant's underlying conviction and the bare allegation that appellant had a prior sex conviction without a full consideration of the statutory factors. After appellant's constitutional challenges to the sexual predator statute were summarily overruled, the court held that insufficient evidence was presented to support the determination by clear and convincing evidence that appellant was likely to engage in the future in one or more sexually oriented offenses.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed in part and remanded because prosecution failed to present the trial court with clear and convincing evidence that appellant was likely to engage in the future in one or more sexually oriented offenses.

 

400 of 2888 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kennedy


Case No. 99 CA 2472


COURT OF APPEALS OF OHIO, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, ROSS COUNTY


1999 Ohio App. LEXIS 4715



September 30, 1999, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [*1] JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant appealed the judgment of conviction and sentence entered by the Chillicothe Municipal Court (Ohio), finding appellant guilty of possessing a controlled substance in violation of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2925.11(A), a minor misdemeanor.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of possessing a controlled substance in violation of Ohio Rev. Code Ann. § 2925.11(A), a minor misdemeanor. The initial stop of appellant's vehicle constituted a constitutionally permissible Terry stop. There was nothing in the police officer's testimony to suggest that the violation of the traffic ordinance was used as a mere pretext to stop appellant and search his van. There was nothing constitutionally suspect in appellant's contact with police subsequent to the stop. The officer's testimony that appellant's pat-down was given in order to check for weapons and ensure the safety of the investigating officers was minimally sufficient to explain and justify the pat-down. Before the pat-down was even conducted, a drug sniffing dog had already alerted police to the smell of drugs. Testimony that the officer found the baggie containing illegal substances was lawfully seized under the plain feel doctrine.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; the stop of appellant's vehicle was constitutionally permissible, appellant's pat-down was not improper and the baggie found was lawfully seized under the plain feel doctrine.
